<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">In this paper, we present the extension of a recently published two-frequency continuous-wave (CW) ultra-high-frequency RF identification ranging technique to multiple carriers. The proposed system concept relies on exact phase information; hence, the passive tag cannot be accurately modeled as a frequency-flat linear device. A linearized model of the tag's reflection coefficient is devised to bridge the gap between the nonlinear reality and the linear CW radar theory. Estimation error bounds are derived and effects caused by noise and multipath propagation are analyzed in detail. It has been found that systematic errors introduced by the tag's reflection characteristic cannot be compensated by using multiple carriers due to large variations caused by detuning. Nonetheless the system, while being vulnerable to multipath propagation effects, still performs well under line-of-sight conditions; mean average errors below 15% of the true distance are possible in typical fading environments..</div>

It is shown that the concept is ideally suited for transponder and secondary radar systems with outstanding performance. A switched injection-locked oscillator transponder can produce an approximately phase coherent high-power response to an interrogating signal and, consequently, allows for long-range transponder systems and precise distance measurement between the reader and transponder. <div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>The Automatic and simultaneous identification, localization, and tracking of targets using electromagnetic radiation started mainly as a military application in radar systems. In the early 1970s, commercial tracking of large and expensive goods emerged, followed by smaller items by the end of the 20th Century <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. Since then, RF identification (RFID) became almost ubiquitous in commercial applications, e.g., tracking and identification of goods or electronic article surveillance.</p><p>Although estimating distances to tagged items is not a new idea in itself, it is a relatively new field of interest in passive ultra-high-frequency (UHF) RFID. Recent work combines the need for a continuous carrier (to power the tag) with range estimation, employing well-known principles like continuous-wave (CW) radar <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>. The application of multiple carriers is also not a new idea in UHF RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>.</p><p>The restrictive spectral masks enforced by existing regulations are a major reason for using narrowband systems like amplitude modulation CW radar for ranging (cf. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>). Wideband systems like frequency modulation CW radar and ultra-wideband (UWB) systems <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a> would require considerable modifications to existing regulations.</p><p>

The assumption of short-time stationary power <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-26" role="math" style="width: 5.493em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.368em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.326em 1004.37em 2.715em -999.997em); top: -2.245em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.136em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-29" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-30" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">κ</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-32" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.268em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-33" style="padding-left: 0.268em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.128em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.112em 1000.73em 4.17em -999.997em); top: -3.965em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-34" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.136em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.833em; left: 0.665em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-35"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-36"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-37" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">κ</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.972em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.252em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.413em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.421em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">P(\kappa)=P_{\kappa}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> completes the linearization.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> This study completes the theoretical background of the recently published two-frequency continuous wave (2FCW) radar approach for passive UHF RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. This ranging system is also extended to multiple carriers in an effort to minimize errors introduced by noise, multipath propagation, and tag variations. The resulting multifrequency continuous-wave (MFCW) ranging approach is evaluated under typical UHF RFID environmental conditions.<p></p><p>In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, a linearized model of the tag's reflection coefficient during backscatter modulation is introduced. This model is applied in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a> to derive the signals used for MFCW ranging, followed by the derivation of a distance estimate out of multiple carriers and a discussion of detuning effects in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>. <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a> contains detailed noise and multipath propagation influence analyses. The ranging system concept is verified using a wideband UHF RFID system-level simulator <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a> in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec6" class="fulltext-link">Section VI</a>. Finally, the findings are summarized in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec7" class="fulltext-link">Section VII</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Linear Model of the Tag Modulation</h2></div><p>On the physical level, a tag modulates data by varying a modulation impedance. The reflection coefficient during this process depends on the chip impedance, which itself depends on the chip input power. This dependence causes the reflection coefficient to be nonlinear. Moreover, the interaction between the time-variant impedances creates a curved transition trajectory in the complex plane (cf. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>). Tag detuning can be interpreted as additional impedance, thus having a direct influence on the reflection coefficient as well.</p><p>As a first step, the linearization neglects everything but the end points of this curve, introducing a center value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-38" role="math" style="width: 3.486em; padding-left: 0.183em;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-45" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">\rho(\omega,P)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a difference value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-46" role="math" style="width: 4.447em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-56"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-57" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; The superposition principle is also applicable due to the linearity of this model, which will be exploited to calculate the backscattered signal for multiple carriers in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Derivation of Amplitude and Phase Relations</h2></div><p>The derivations outlined in this section are based on the signal model shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a> and done in the complex baseband. The entire derivation assumes short-time stationarity.

width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1676" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">⋅</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1677" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">(</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1678" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1679"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1688"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1689"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1690" style="font-size: 50%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1691" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1692"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1694"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1695"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1696" style="font-size: 50%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1697" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">)</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1698" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">]</span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.805em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.838em 1001.68em 0.483em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.68em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -3.961em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(13)}}$"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1594"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1595"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1596"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1597"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1598"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-1599"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1600"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-1601" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(13)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-66">c_{n-{\rm M}}:={1\over 2}A_{n}\widetilde{H}_{n}\widetilde{H}_{n-{\rm M}}G_{n-{\rm M}}\Delta\rho_{n}e^{-\jmath\left[\phi_{\rm M}+\tau\cdot(2\omega_{c}+2\omega_{n}-\omega_{\rm M})\right]}\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">c_{n-{\rm M}}:={1\over 2}A_{n}\widetilde{H}_{n}\widetilde{H}_{n-{\rm M}}G_{n-{\rm M}}\Delta\rho_{n}e^{-\jmath\left[\phi_{\rm M}+\tau\cdot(2\omega_{c}+2\omega_{n}-\omega_{\rm M})\right]}\eqno{\hbox{(13)}}</span></span></disp-formula>for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">n=1,\ldots, N_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1699" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1700"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1701" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1702" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-1703" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">1</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1704" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1705" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">…</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1706" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">,</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1707" style="padding-left: 0.183em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.9em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1708" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1709"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1710"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1711" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">n=1,\ldots, N_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Estimates of these amplitudes are used by MFCW ranging to determine the distance to the tag.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>MFCW Distance Estimate</h2></div><p>The set of lower and upper sideband phases <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle c_{n+{\rm M}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1712" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1713"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1714" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">∠</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1715"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1716" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1717"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1718"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1719" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1720" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">+</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1721"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1722"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1723" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">\angle c_{n+{\rm M}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle c_{n-{\rm M}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1724" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1725"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1726" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">∠</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1727"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.105em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1728" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.423em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1729"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1730"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1731" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1732" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1733"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1734"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1735" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">\angle c_{n-{\rm M}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> form a system of equations that is solved for the desired delay <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\tau</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1736" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1737"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1738" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">τ<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">\tau</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Estimation based on the received signal strength (RSS) is also possible, but not in the scope of this paper.</p><p>The tag modulation phase shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{\rm M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1739" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1740"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1741"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.6em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1742" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϕ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1743"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1744"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1745" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">\phi_{\rm M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is typically unknown and cannot be controlled by an interrogator or tag. It is thus assumed to be uniformly distributed between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">-\pi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1746" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1747"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1748" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1749" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">π<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">-\pi</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pi</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1750" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1751"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1752" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">π<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">\pi</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Since <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega_{c}\gg\omega_{n}\gg\omega_{\rm M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1753" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1754"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1755"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1756" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1757"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1758"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1759" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1760" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≫</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1761" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.144em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1762" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1763"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1764"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1765" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">n</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-1766" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">≫</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1767" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1768" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1769"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1770"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1771" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">\omega_{c}\gg\omega_{n}\gg\omega_{\rm M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, a direct solution of this system of equations leads to an ill-conditioned problem. Therefore, we subtract the phase shifts in order to eliminate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\phi_{\rm M}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1772" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1773"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1774"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.324em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.6em 4.387em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1775" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ϕ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1776"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1777"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1778" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">M</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">\phi_{\rm M}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1779" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1780"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1781"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1782" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ω</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-1783"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1784"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-1785" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">\omega_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> beforehand. This cannot be achieved by combining upper and lower sidebands, hence, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">c_{n+{\rm M}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1786" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-1787"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-1788"><span style="display: inline-block;
