padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2341" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">∠</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2342" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-2343"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2344" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ρ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-2345"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2346"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-2347" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">1</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2348" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Δ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-2349"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.48em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-2350" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">ρ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.547em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.321em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-2351"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2352"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-2353" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">∗</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.366em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.721em; left: 0.544em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-2354"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2355"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-2356" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.18em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-2364"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2365"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(4.688em 1000em 5.048em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 23.426em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.847em 1000em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.18em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-2366"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2367"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.805em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.057em 1001.68em 1.324em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.68em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -3.18em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-2357"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2358"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-2359"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2360"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-2361"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2362"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-2363" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(16)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-93">\eqalignno{\angle c_{1+{\rm M}}c_{2+{\rm M}}^{\ast}=\angle c_{1-{\rm M}}c_{2-{\rm M}}^{\ast}=2\tau(\omega_{2}-\omega_{1})+\angle\Delta\rho_{1}\Delta\rho_{2}^{\ast}\cr&amp;&amp;{\hbox{(16)}}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{\angle c_{1+{\rm M}}c_{2+{\rm M}}^{\ast}=\angle c_{1-{\rm M}}c_{2-{\rm M}}^{\ast}=2\tau(\omega_{2}-\omega_{1})+\angle\Delta\rho_{1}\Delta\rho_{2}^{\ast}\cr&amp;&amp;{\hbox{(16)}}}</span></span></disp-formula>and the distance estimate is <disp-formula id="deqn17" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{d}=\underbrace{\tau c}_{d}+\underbrace{c\cdot\angle\Delta\rho_{1}\Delta\rho_{2}^{\ast}\over 2(\omega_{2}-\omega_{1})}_{{\rm error}\ {\rm caused}\ {\rm by}\ {\rm tag}}.\eqno{\hbox{(17)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-94-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-94">\mathhat{d}=\underbrace{\tau c}_{d}+\underbrace{c\cdot\angle\Delta\rho_{1}\Delta\rho_{2}^{\ast}\over 2(\omega_{2}-\omega_{1})}_{{\rm error}\ {\rm caused}\ {\rm by}\ {\rm tag}}.\eqno{\hbox{(17)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\mathhat{d}=\underbrace{\tau c}_{d}+\underbrace{c\cdot\angle\Delta\rho_{1}\Delta\rho_{2}^{\ast}\over 2(\omega_{2}-\omega_{1})}_{{\rm error}\ {\rm caused}\ {\rm by}\ {\rm tag}}.\eqno{\hbox{(17)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>The error term introduced by the tag causes the distance estimate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-95-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-95">\mathhat{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to be biased.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. On Mitigation of the Systematic Error Caused by the Tag</h3><p>The bias in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn17" href="#deqn17" class="fulltext-link">(17)</a> depends on frequency, power, and detuning. Exemplarily, this influence on the mean absolute error (MAE) of 2FCW ranging is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. Detuning plus assembly impedance is varied from −70% to 400% from the optimal value for this plot. We used an AWGN channel with single-sided noise density <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{0}=-82\ {\hbox{dBm/Hz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-96-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-96">N_{0}=-82\ {\hbox{dBm/Hz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and an estimation window size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N=144432</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-97-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-97">N=144432</script></tex-math></inline-formula> samples. The carriers were set to 3.2 W/32 mW effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP) at a center frequency of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\omega_{c}=910\ {\hbox{MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-98-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-98">\omega_{c}=910\ {\hbox{MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with 0-Hz offset for the primary (energy) carrier. Note that the maximum range of detuned tags is considerably lower than 7 m; only functional tags are taken into account. The background of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a> contains a histogram of the MAE, while the foreground shows the average MAE. We have chosen a strong secondary carrier to minimize the influence of noise in these plots.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Influence of detuning on the MAE for 2FCW ranging at frequency offsets of 1 and 10 MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>While noise is still an issue compared to the systematic bias for a frequency offset of 1 MHz and distances of &gt;2 m, it is almost negligible for 10-MHz offset. The maximum MAE was approximately 40–50 cm for both plots, while the average MAE does not exceed 10 cm.</p><p>Effective removal of this error is a nontrivial task and yet unresolved. The tag is designed to work for a frequency range of 860–960 MHz specified in the EPCglobal Class-1 Gen-2 standard <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_4b">[10]</a>. Consequently, its spectral characteristic is a smooth function and a Taylor-series expansion of the phase shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle\Delta\rho_{i}\Delta\rho_{j}^{\ast}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-99-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-99">\angle\Delta\rho_{i}\Delta\rho_{j}^{\ast}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is approximately linear subject to the frequency difference <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-100-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-100">(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for reasonably small carrier offset frequencies. Since the phase shift caused by wave propagation <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">2\tau(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-101-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-101">2\tau(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is also linear with frequency difference, the effects of tag and distance cannot be separated using multiple carriers.</p><p>A characterization of the labels after manufacture and/or after application to the tagged items would tremendously increase costs and is thus not practicable. Moreover, such a characterization would lose its validity if the items are placed near other objects due to changes in the state of detuning. For the same reasons, i.e., the dependence of the error on individual incident power levels and on detuning, reference estimates based on tags at known ranges can only be used to compensate for an approximate average value, not for the true value. If the range of detuning is known, at least an expected average error can be compensated.</p><p>It shall be noted that typical UHF RFID channels are fading channels. The MAE is dominated by multipath propagation effects even in moderate multipath environments, not by detuning (cf. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>).</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Influence of Noise and Multipath Propagation</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5a"><h3>A. Influence of White Noise</h3><p>Analogous to other phase estimators <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_5a">[11]</a> and under the assumption of independent real and imaginary parts, i.e., circular symmetric noise, we can write <disp-formula id="deqn18" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{i}\}={1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{i}}={N_{0}\over N\vert c_{i}\vert^{2}}\eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-102-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-102">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{i}\}={1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{i}}={N_{0}\over N\vert c_{i}\vert^{2}}\eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{i}\}={1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{i}}={N_{0}\over N\vert c_{i}\vert^{2}}\eqno{\hbox{(18)}}</span></span></disp-formula>for the variance of one phase estimate. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-103-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-103">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the length of the estimation window in samples, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{0}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-104-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-104">N_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the single-sided noise density, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\vert c_{i}\vert</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-105-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-105">\vert c_{i}\vert</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the signal (component) amplitude. For the phase difference between two components, we obtain <disp-formula id="deqn19" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{ij}\}={1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{i}}+{1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{j}}+{r_{ij}\over N^{2}\ {\rm SNR}_{i}\ {\rm SNR}_{j}}\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-106-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-106">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{ij}\}={1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{i}}+{1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{j}}+{r_{ij}\over N^{2}\ {\rm SNR}_{i}\ {\rm SNR}_{j}}\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{ij}\}={1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{i}}+{1\over N\ {\rm SNR}_{j}}+{r_{ij}\over N^{2}\ {\rm SNR}_{i}\ {\rm SNR}_{j}}\eqno{\hbox{(19)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">r_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-107-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-107">r_{ij}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the cross covariance between components <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">i</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-108-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-108">i</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">j</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-109-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-109">j</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Typically passive RFID systems are forward-link-limited <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_5a">[1]</a> so signal-to-noise (SNR) values are high. It follows that the quadratic cross correlation term is negligible. Using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn15" href="#deqn15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a> to obtain the distance results in <disp-formula id="deqn20" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}={c^{2}\over 4(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})^{2}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{ij}\}.\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-110-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-110">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}={c^{2}\over 4(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})^{2}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{ij}\}.\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}={c^{2}\over 4(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})^{2}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{\varphi}_{ij}\}.\eqno{\hbox{(20)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>There are <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{c}(N_{c}-1)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-111-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-111">N_{c}(N_{c}-1)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> feasible combinations of phase differences between the sidebands of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-112-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-112">N_{c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> carriers. Averaging all these combinations comes at the cost of correlation between the components. For the conservative approach of using each sideband only once, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor}_{\rm e}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-113-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-113">{\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor}_{\rm e}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> combinations remain, where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor}_{\rm e}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-114-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-114">{\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor}_{\rm e}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> denotes the rounding to the next lower even integer value. For this case, we obtain <disp-formula id="deqn21" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\displaylines{{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\!=\!{c^{2}N_{0}\over 4 N\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor_{\rm e}^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}/2}{\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-1+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\!+\!\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\over\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+1+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}(\omega_{2i}\!-\!\omega_{2i-1})^{2}}\hfill\cr\hfill+{c^{2}N_{0}\over 4 N\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor_{\rm e}^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}/2}{\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-1-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\!+\!\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\over\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+1-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}(\omega_{2i}\!-\!\omega_{2i-1})^{2}}\cr\hfill\hbox{(21)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-115-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-115">\displaylines{{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\!=\!{c^{2}N_{0}\over 4 N\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor_{\rm e}^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}/2}{\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-1+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\!+\!\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\over\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+1+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}(\omega_{2i}\!-\!\omega_{2i-1})^{2}}\hfill\cr\hfill+{c^{2}N_{0}\over 4 N\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor_{\rm e}^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}/2}{\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-1-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\!+\!\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\over\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+1-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}(\omega_{2i}\!-\!\omega_{2i-1})^{2}}\cr\hfill\hbox{(21)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\displaylines{{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\!=\!{c^{2}N_{0}\over 4 N\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor_{\rm e}^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}/2}{\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-1+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\!+\!\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\over\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+1+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+{\rm M}}\vert^{2}(\omega_{2i}\!-\!\omega_{2i-1})^{2}}\hfill\cr\hfill+{c^{2}N_{0}\over 4 N\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor_{\rm e}^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}/2}{\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-1-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\!+\!\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\over\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i+1-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}\vert\mathhat{c}_{2i-{\rm M}}\vert^{2}(\omega_{2i}\!-\!\omega_{2i-1})^{2}}\cr\hfill\hbox{(21)}}</span></span></disp-formula>for the overall variance. Remarkably, we can ignore the correlation between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{d}_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-116-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-116">\mathhat{d}_{ij}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and combine all sidebands in case of equal carrier amplitudes <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{2},\ldots, A_{N_{c}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-117-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-117">A_{2},\ldots, A_{N_{c}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> (<inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">A_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-118-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-118">A_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can be arbitrary) and equal frequency spacings, obtaining an approximation <disp-formula id="deqn22" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\approx{1\over N_{c}^{2}(N_{c}-1)^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}}\sum_{j=1\atop j\neq i}^{N_{c}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\eqno{\hbox{(22)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-119-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-119">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\approx{1\over N_{c}^{2}(N_{c}-1)^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}}\sum_{j=1\atop j\neq i}^{N_{c}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\eqno{\hbox{(22)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\approx{1\over N_{c}^{2}(N_{c}-1)^{2}}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}}\sum_{j=1\atop j\neq i}^{N_{c}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\eqno{\hbox{(22)}}</span></span></disp-formula>with <disp-formula id="deqn23" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{d}_{ij}\vert_{i&gt;j}={c\over 2}\cdot{\angle\mathhat{c}_{i+{\rm M}}\mathhat{c}_{j+{\rm M}}^{\ast}\over(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})}\quad\mathhat{d}_{ij}\vert_{i&lt;j}={c\over 2}\cdot{\angle\mathhat{c}_{i-{\rm M}}\mathhat{c}_{j-{\rm M}}^{\ast}\over(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})}.\eqno{\hbox{(23)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-120-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-120">\mathhat{d}_{ij}\vert_{i&gt;j}={c\over 2}\cdot{\angle\mathhat{c}_{i+{\rm M}}\mathhat{c}_{j+{\rm M}}^{\ast}\over(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})}\quad\mathhat{d}_{ij}\vert_{i&lt;j}={c\over 2}\cdot{\angle\mathhat{c}_{i-{\rm M}}\mathhat{c}_{j-{\rm M}}^{\ast}\over(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})}.\eqno{\hbox{(23)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\mathhat{d}_{ij}\vert_{i&gt;j}={c\over 2}\cdot{\angle\mathhat{c}_{i+{\rm M}}\mathhat{c}_{j+{\rm M}}^{\ast}\over(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})}\quad\mathhat{d}_{ij}\vert_{i&lt;j}={c\over 2}\cdot{\angle\mathhat{c}_{i-{\rm M}}\mathhat{c}_{j-{\rm M}}^{\ast}\over(\omega_{j}-\omega_{i})}.\eqno{\hbox{(23)}}</span></span></disp-formula>Clearly, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{c}^{2}(N_{c}-1)^{2}\gg{\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor}_{\rm e}^{2}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-121-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-121">N_{c}^{2}(N_{c}-1)^{2}\gg{\lfloor N_{c}\rfloor}_{\rm e}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{c}&gt;2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-122-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-122">N_{c}&gt;2</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, thus the resulting variance is considerable lower if all sidebands are combined and the correlation can be neglected. The average component variance in such a system is approximately equal to the individual secondary carrier variances because of the strong primary (energy) carrier <disp-formula id="deqn24" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{{\hskip-20pt}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{23}\}=&amp;\,{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{32}\}={\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{34}\}=\ldots\cr\approx&amp;\,\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}={1\over N_{c}(N_{c}-1)}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}}\sum_{j=1\atop j\neq i}^{N_{c}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}&amp;\hbox{(24)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-123-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-123">\eqalignno{{\hskip-20pt}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{23}\}=&amp;\,{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{32}\}={\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{34}\}=\ldots\cr\approx&amp;\,\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}={1\over N_{c}(N_{c}-1)}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}}\sum_{j=1\atop j\neq i}^{N_{c}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}&amp;\hbox{(24)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{{\hskip-20pt}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{23}\}=&amp;\,{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{32}\}={\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{34}\}=\ldots\cr\approx&amp;\,\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}={1\over N_{c}(N_{c}-1)}\sum_{i=1}^{N_{c}}\sum_{j=1\atop j\neq i}^{N_{c}}{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}&amp;\hbox{(24)}}</span></span></disp-formula>It follows that the best achievable variance scaling for multiple carriers is <disp-formula id="deqn25" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\vert_{\rm MFCW}\approx{\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\over N_{c}(N_{c}-1)}.\eqno{\hbox{(25)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-124-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-124">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\vert_{\rm MFCW}\approx{\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\over N_{c}(N_{c}-1)}.\eqno{\hbox{(25)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\vert_{\rm MFCW}\approx{\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\over N_{c}(N_{c}-1)}.\eqno{\hbox{(25)}}</span></span></disp-formula>while the largest possible frequency offset is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N_{c}\Delta\omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-125-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-125">N_{c}\Delta\omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\Delta\omega</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-126-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-126">\Delta\omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> being the frequency spacing. If this offset is chosen for 2FCW, according to <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn15" href="#deqn15" class="fulltext-link">(15)</a>, its variance scales with <disp-formula id="deqn26" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\vert_{2{\rm FCW}}\approx{\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\over N_{c}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(26)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-127-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-127">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\vert_{2{\rm FCW}}\approx{\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\over N_{c}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(26)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}\}\vert_{2{\rm FCW}}\approx{\overline{\rm var}\{\mathhat{d}_{ij}\}\over N_{c}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(26)}}</span></span></disp-formula>which is lower than the multicarrier's variance. Simulations have shown that the correlation can be used to reduce the variance caused by noise slightly below this level for multicarrier systems.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5b"><h3>B. Influence of Multipath Propagation</h3><p>In case of multipath propagation, the stochastic channel phase term <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle\widetilde{H}_{i}\widetilde{H}_{i\pm{\rm M}}\widetilde{H}_{j}^{\ast}\widetilde{H}_{j\pm{\rm M}}^{\ast}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-128-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-128">\angle\widetilde{H}_{i}\widetilde{H}_{i\pm{\rm M}}\widetilde{H}_{j}^{\ast}\widetilde{H}_{j\pm{\rm M}}^{\ast}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn14" href="#deqn14" class="fulltext-link">(14)</a> is nonzero. We start our analysis with one channel, assuming given channel gains <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\widetilde{H}_{i},\widetilde{H}_{j}\sim{\cal CN}(m,\sigma^{2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-129-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-129">\widetilde{H}_{i},\widetilde{H}_{j}\sim{\cal CN}(m,\sigma^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, circular symmetric around the mean value. This assumption implies a Ricean fading channel with line-of-sight (LOS) amplitude <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">m</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-130-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-130">m</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and is valid for a small frequency spacing. We assume a pure smallscale channel here to strip the tilde and define the covariance matrix <disp-formula id="deqn27" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\underline{\mmb h}^{H}\}-{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\}{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\}^{H}=\left[\matrix{\sigma^{2}&amp;\beta\cr\beta^{\ast}&amp;\sigma^{2}}\right]\eqno{\hbox{(27)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-131-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-131">{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\underline{\mmb h}^{H}\}-{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\}{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\}^{H}=\left[\matrix{\sigma^{2}&amp;\beta\cr\beta^{\ast}&amp;\sigma^{2}}\right]\eqno{\hbox{(27)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\underline{\mmb h}^{H}\}-{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\}{\rm E}\{\underline{\mmb h}\}^{H}=\left[\matrix{\sigma^{2}&amp;\beta\cr\beta^{\ast}&amp;\sigma^{2}}\right]\eqno{\hbox{(27)}}</span></span></disp-formula>with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\underline{\mmb h}=[H_{i}\ H_{j}]^{T}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-132-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-132">\underline{\mmb h}=[H_{i}\ H_{j}]^{T}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The superscript <sup><i>H</i></sup> denotes the Hermitian transpose.</p><p>We are evaluating <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle H_{i}-\angle H_{j}=\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-133-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-133">\angle H_{i}-\angle H_{j}=\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for the distance estimate, which is approximately <disp-formula id="deqn28" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}={\rm arctan}\left({{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\over{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}}\right)\approx{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\over{\rm E}\left\{{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}}\eqno{\hbox{(28)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-134-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-134">\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}={\rm arctan}\left({{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\over{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}}\right)\approx{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\over{\rm E}\left\{{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}}\eqno{\hbox{(28)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}={\rm arctan}\left({{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\over{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}}\right)\approx{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\over{\rm E}\left\{{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}}\eqno{\hbox{(28)}}</span></span></disp-formula>for LOS scenarios with a high Ricean K-factor. Thus, <disp-formula id="deqn29" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\left\{\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\approx{{\rm var}\left\{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}\over{\rm E}\left\{{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(29)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-135-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-135">{\rm var}\left\{\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\approx{{\rm var}\left\{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}\over{\rm E}\left\{{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(29)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\left\{\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\approx{{\rm var}\left\{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}\over{\rm E}\left\{{\rm Re}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}^{2}}.\eqno{\hbox{(29)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p><p>After some short derivations using the properties of complex Gaussian processes <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref12" id="context_ref_12_5b">[12]</a>, we obtain <disp-formula id="deqn30-31" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{{\hskip-15pt}{\rm E}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\!=\!&amp;\,\beta\!+\!\vert m\vert^{2}&amp;\hbox{(30)}\cr{\hskip-15pt}{\rm var}\left\{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}\!=\!&amp;\,{1\over 2}{\rm Re}\left\{\sigma^{4}\!-\!\beta^{2}\!+\!2\vert m\vert^{2}(\sigma^{2}\!-\!\beta)\right\}&amp;\hbox{(31)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-136-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-136">\eqalignno{{\hskip-15pt}{\rm E}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\!=\!&amp;\,\beta\!+\!\vert m\vert^{2}&amp;\hbox{(30)}\cr{\hskip-15pt}{\rm var}\left\{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}\!=\!&amp;\,{1\over 2}{\rm Re}\left\{\sigma^{4}\!-\!\beta^{2}\!+\!2\vert m\vert^{2}(\sigma^{2}\!-\!\beta)\right\}&amp;\hbox{(31)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{{\hskip-15pt}{\rm E}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\!=\!&amp;\,\beta\!+\!\vert m\vert^{2}&amp;\hbox{(30)}\cr{\hskip-15pt}{\rm var}\left\{{\rm Im}\left\{H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\right\}\!=\!&amp;\,{1\over 2}{\rm Re}\left\{\sigma^{4}\!-\!\beta^{2}\!+\!2\vert m\vert^{2}(\sigma^{2}\!-\!\beta)\right\}&amp;\hbox{(31)}}</span></span></disp-formula>and, thus, <disp-formula id="deqn32" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm var}\left\{\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\approx{{\rm Re}\left\{\sigma^{4}-\beta^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}(\sigma^{2}-\beta)\right\}\over 2{\rm Re}\left\{\beta+\vert m\vert^{2}\right\}^{2}}\eqno{\hbox{(32)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-137-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-137">{\rm var}\left\{\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\approx{{\rm Re}\left\{\sigma^{4}-\beta^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}(\sigma^{2}-\beta)\right\}\over 2{\rm Re}\left\{\beta+\vert m\vert^{2}\right\}^{2}}\eqno{\hbox{(32)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm var}\left\{\angle H_{i}H_{j}^{\ast}\right\}\approx{{\rm Re}\left\{\sigma^{4}-\beta^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}(\sigma^{2}-\beta)\right\}\over 2{\rm Re}\left\{\beta+\vert m\vert^{2}\right\}^{2}}\eqno{\hbox{(32)}}</span></span></disp-formula>which is the variance caused by one channel.</p><p>Introducing a second channel, we have to deal with <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}H_{j}^{\ast}H_{j\pm{\rm M}}^{\ast}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-138-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-138">\angle H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}H_{j}^{\ast}H_{j\pm{\rm M}}^{\ast}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> instead of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\angle H_{i}H_{j\pm{\rm M}}^{\ast}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-139-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-139">\angle H_{i}H_{j\pm{\rm M}}^{\ast}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is a lot more complicated to handle. The problem becomes simple if we assume that the product <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-140-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-140">H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is also approximately Gaussian with new variance and mean value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}\sim{\cal CN}(\widetilde{m},\widetilde{\sigma}^{2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-141-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-141">H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}\sim{\cal CN}(\widetilde{m},\widetilde{\sigma}^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In this case, the above derivations apply to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-142-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-142">H_{i}H_{i\pm{\rm M}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as well. This assumption of Gaussianity holds for LOS scenarios with a high K-factor <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\hbox{K}}\gtrsim 10\ {\hbox{dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-143-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-143">{\hbox{K}}\gtrsim 10\ {\hbox{dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Exploiting the properties of complex Gaussian processes again, it can easily be shown that <disp-formula id="deqn33" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\widetilde{m}=m^{2} \quad\widetilde{\sigma}^{2}=2\sigma^{2}\left(\sigma^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right) \quad\widetilde{\beta}=2\beta\left(\beta+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(33)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-144-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-144">\widetilde{m}=m^{2} \quad\widetilde{\sigma}^{2}=2\sigma^{2}\left(\sigma^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right) \quad\widetilde{\beta}=2\beta\left(\beta+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(33)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\widetilde{m}=m^{2} \quad\widetilde{\sigma}^{2}=2\sigma^{2}\left(\sigma^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right) \quad\widetilde{\beta}=2\beta\left(\beta+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(33)}}</span></span></disp-formula>for identical uplink and downlink channels and <disp-formula id="deqn34" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\widetilde{m}=m^{2} \quad\widetilde{\sigma}^{2}=\sigma^{2}\left(\sigma^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right) \quad\widetilde{\beta}=\beta\left(\beta+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(34)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-145-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-145">\widetilde{m}=m^{2} \quad\widetilde{\sigma}^{2}=\sigma^{2}\left(\sigma^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right) \quad\widetilde{\beta}=\beta\left(\beta+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(34)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\widetilde{m}=m^{2} \quad\widetilde{\sigma}^{2}=\sigma^{2}\left(\sigma^{2}+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right) \quad\widetilde{\beta}=\beta\left(\beta+2\vert m\vert^{2}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(34)}}</span></span></disp-formula>for distinct channels under this assumption.</p><p>The simplest way to obtain the variance for the combination of multiple carriers is to use the average frequency shift to calculate the covariance matrix. This approach is possible because of the small frequency spacings up to a few megahertz. Direct application of <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn21" href="#deqn21" class="fulltext-link">(21)</a> is not possible due to heavy correlation between the phase estimates.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec5c"><h3>C. Mae</h3><p>The expected MAE of the proposed ranging system concept can be expressed by mean and standard deviation of the calculated estimate. We assume a Gaussian distribution for the distance estimate <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{d}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-146-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-146">\mathhat{d}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is approximately true for LOS scenarios, i.e., high Ricean K-factors. Applying this assumption, the deviation from the true value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-147-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-147">d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is also Gaussian with mean value <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu:={\rm E}\{\mathhat{d}\}-d</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-148-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-148">\mu:={\rm E}\{\mathhat{d}\}-d</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the MAE is <disp-formula id="deqn35" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{{\rm MAE}\{\mathhat{d}\}=&amp;\,{\rm E}\left\{\vert\mathhat{d}-d\vert\right\}\cr=&amp;\,{1\over\sigma\sqrt{2\pi}}\int\limits_{-\infty}^{\infty}\vert x-\mu\vert e^{-{x^{2}\over 2\sigma^{2}}}dx\cr=&amp;\,\sqrt{2\over\pi}\sigma e^{-{\mu^{2}\over 2\sigma^{2}}}+\mu{\rm erf}\left\{{\mu\over\sqrt{2}\sigma}\right\}&amp;\hbox{(35)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-149-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-149">\eqalignno{{\rm MAE}\{\mathhat{d}\}=&amp;\,{\rm E}\left\{\vert\mathhat{d}-d\vert\right\}\cr=&amp;\,{1\over\sigma\sqrt{2\pi}}\int\limits_{-\infty}^{\infty}\vert x-\mu\vert e^{-{x^{2}\over 2\sigma^{2}}}dx\cr=&amp;\,\sqrt{2\over\pi}\sigma e^{-{\mu^{2}\over 2\sigma^{2}}}+\mu{\rm erf}\left\{{\mu\over\sqrt{2}\sigma}\right\}&amp;\hbox{(35)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\eqalignno{{\rm MAE}\{\mathhat{d}\}=&amp;\,{\rm E}\left\{\vert\mathhat{d}-d\vert\right\}\cr=&amp;\,{1\over\sigma\sqrt{2\pi}}\int\limits_{-\infty}^{\infty}\vert x-\mu\vert e^{-{x^{2}\over 2\sigma^{2}}}dx\cr=&amp;\,\sqrt{2\over\pi}\sigma e^{-{\mu^{2}\over 2\sigma^{2}}}+\mu{\rm erf}\left\{{\mu\over\sqrt{2}\sigma}\right\}&amp;\hbox{(35)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm erf}\{\alpha\}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-150-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-150">{\rm erf}\{\alpha\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the error function <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_5c">[13]</a> <disp-formula id="deqn36" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm erf}\{\alpha\}={2\over\sqrt{\pi}}\int\limits_{0}^{\alpha}e^{-x^{2}}dx.\eqno{\hbox{(36)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-151-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-151">{\rm erf}\{\alpha\}={2\over\sqrt{\pi}}\int\limits_{0}^{\alpha}e^{-x^{2}}dx.\eqno{\hbox{(36)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">{\rm erf}\{\alpha\}={2\over\sqrt{\pi}}\int\limits_{0}^{\alpha}e^{-x^{2}}dx.\eqno{\hbox{(36)}}</span></span></disp-formula></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec6"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VI.</div><h2>Simulations</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6a"><h3>A. Simulator Setup</h3><p>The theoretical results given in this paper have been verified by simulations using a wideband interrogator/tag simulation tool <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_6a">[8]</a>. It is based on behavioral models of tag and interrogator building blocks and partially implements the EPCglobal Class-1 Gen-2 protocol <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_6a">[10]</a>.</p><p>The simulator was configured as follows: carrier frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{c}=910\ {\hbox{MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-152-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-152">f_{c}=910\ {\hbox{MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, tag clock frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm clk}=1.92\ {\hbox{MHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-153-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-153">f_{\rm clk}=1.92\ {\hbox{MHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and modulation frequency <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{\rm M}=48\ {\hbox{kHz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-154-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-154">f_{\rm M}=48\ {\hbox{kHz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with an unknown uniformly distributed phase shift <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\varphi_{\rm M}\in[-\pi,\pi]</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-155-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-155">\varphi_{\rm M}\in[-\pi,\pi]</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. Unless otherwise stated, transmit power of the primary (energy) carrier <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">n=1</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-156-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-156">n=1</script></tex-math></inline-formula> was set to 3.2 W EIRP at a frequency offset of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{1}=0\ {\hbox{Hz}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-157-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-157">f_{1}=0\ {\hbox{Hz}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, while secondary (ranging) carriers were set to 320 <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu{\hbox{W}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-158-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-158">\mu{\hbox{W}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> EIRP. The average direct feedback gain was chosen to be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\rm E}\{K_{n}\}=-30\ {\hbox{dB}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-159-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-159">{\rm E}\{K_{n}\}=-30\ {\hbox{dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> with an average delay of 3 ns; the sampling window size was set to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N=144432</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-160-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-160">N=144432</script></tex-math></inline-formula> samples for all simulations. Systematic errors that could be corrected by the interrogator in real-world applications are perfectly compensated.</p><p>The simulator results in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5</a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link"></a><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link"></a>–<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">9</a> were calculated by averaging 250 independent estimates per marker. Four-frequency continuous-wave (4FCW) ranging was performed by comparing the phases of carriers 1/2 and 3/4 (each carrier used only once).</p><p>All simulated multipath channels are based on a short-range indoor smallscale channel model <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref14" id="context_ref_14_6a">[14]</a>, resulting in Ricean fading. Uplink and downlink channels were chosen to be identical (worst case, cf. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>). All multipath simulations, except for <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 4</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">9</a>, where a light fading channel was desired, used a logarithmically dropping Ricean K-factor with 30 dB at 0 m and 10 dB at 5 m. The root mean square (rms) delay spread increased logarithmically from 1 to 20 ns in the same range. This channel setup reflects the values given in the literature for the UHF RFID frequency band (cf. <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_6a">[9]</a> and <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref15" id="context_ref_15_6a">[15]</a>). We extended the range to 7 m for the light fading channel, approximately resulting in an rms delay spread of 1–10 ns and a Ricean K-factor of 30-15 dB within 0–5 m. Additive white noise was set to −82 dBm/Hz after sampling at the reader input stage.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Example comparison between analytical and simulation results for a weakly fading channel.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec6b"><h3>B. Simulation Results</h3><p>The proposed ranging method was tested under various conditions of which only a small selection of simulations can be presented here.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows a comparison of theory and simulations for 2FCW radar using a frequency spacing of 8 MHz. In this simulation a detuned tag (+100% of the optimal impedance) moves from 30 cm to 6 m in the light multipath environment, while the interrogator continuously estimates its range. The expected average deviation using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn17" href="#deqn17" class="fulltext-link">(17)</a> and 68/99.7% intervals applying the results in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a> are also displayed for comparison. As can be seen, the ranging performs within expected parameters.</p><p>The MAE in AWGN and fading environments for different carrier setups is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Figs. 5</a> and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">6</a>, respectively. Setup 2 uses the standard power setup, while the secondary carrier power is increased to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">P_{2\ldots 4}=32\ {\hbox{mW}}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-161-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-161">P_{2\ldots 4}=32\ {\hbox{mW}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for Setup 1. All simulations assume a well-tuned tag; frequency setups are given in the captions. The small deviations from the expected analytical values given in this paper are caused by overlapping harmonics due to nonideal filters and residual filter transients. The results show that the performance depends primarily on the largest frequency offset. Moreover, noise is negligible compared to the errors caused by multipath propagation.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Mean absolute distance error caused by <b>noise and the bias introduced by the tag</b> for 2FCW <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(N_{c}=2)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-162-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-162">(N_{c}=2)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 4FCW <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(N_{c}=4)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-163-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-163">(N_{c}=4)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>: analytical results versus simulation for two different carrier setups. Carrier offset frequencies <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{n}=0, 3, 1, 2</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-164-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-164">f_{n}=0, 3, 1, 2</script></tex-math></inline-formula> MHz (setup 1) and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{n}=0, 4, 2, 10</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-165-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-165">f_{n}=0, 4, 2, 10</script></tex-math></inline-formula> MHz (setup 2).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Mean absolute distance error caused by <b>multipath propagation</b> for 2FCW <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(N_{c}=2)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-166-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-166">(N_{c}=2)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and 4FCW <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(N_{c}=4)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-167-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-167">(N_{c}=4)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>: analytical results versus simulation for two different carrier setups. Carrier offset frequencies <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{n}=0, 6, 2, 4</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-168-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-168">f_{n}=0, 6, 2, 4</script></tex-math></inline-formula> MHz (setup 1) and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{n}=0, 12, 2, 6</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-169-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-169">f_{n}=0, 12, 2, 6</script></tex-math></inline-formula> MHz (setup 2).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>A special property of the proposed ranging system is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a>. The MAE for multipath propagation drops for an increased frequency spacing, as long as the channel features a significant LOS component. The maximum frequency offset is bounded by phase ambiguities at one quarter of the wavelength. We thus suggest to select the frequency offset of a 2FCW system such that <disp-formula id="deqn37" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{2}-f_{1}\lesssim{c\over 4(d_{\max}+3\sigma)}\eqno{\hbox{(37)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-170-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-170">f_{2}-f_{1}\lesssim{c\over 4(d_{\max}+3\sigma)}\eqno{\hbox{(37)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">f_{2}-f_{1}\lesssim{c\over 4(d_{\max}+3\sigma)}\eqno{\hbox{(37)}}</span></span></disp-formula>where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">c</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-171-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-171">c</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the speed of light, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">d_{\rm max}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-172-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-172">d_{\rm max}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the maximum distance, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sigma</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-173-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-173">\sigma</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the standard deviation caused by the channel. This minimizes the influence of noise and multipath propagation while still avoiding phase ambiguities.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Analytical mean absolute distance error caused by multipath propagation for 2FCW <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(N_{c}=2)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-174-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-174">(N_{c}=2)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> versus frequency spacing <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{2}-f_{1}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-175-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-175">f_{2}-f_{1}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> for four different channels. Uplink/downlink channels are identical (worst case).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>An undesired effect is caused by the combination of backscatter communication with identical receive/transmit (RX/TX) antenna at the interrogator. This combination creates identical uplink and downlink channels, increasing the fading range and the error rate of MFCW ranging, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. This simulation uses offset frequencies of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{n}=0, 12</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-176-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-176">f_{n}=0, 12</script></tex-math></inline-formula> MHz and identical parameters per uplink and downlink channel. Analytical results are given in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Mean absolute distance error caused by <b>multipath propagation</b> for 2FCW <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(N_{c}=2)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-177-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-177">(N_{c}=2)</script></tex-math></inline-formula> using a well-tuned tag: analytical results versus simulation for identical and independent uplink/downlink channels.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>A direct comparison between the errors caused by noise, multipath propagation, and the bias introducted by the tag's phase shift can be found in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>. We set up a simulation using only a moderate multipath channel with high K-factor and low rms delay spread for this plot. The tag is detuned by +100% of the optimal impedance, which approximately maximizes the influence of the bias on the MAE. Further detuning flattens the reflection coefficient and thus reduces the introduced error. It can be seen that the bias is dominant in the AWGN case, while it is almost negligible in the presence of multipath propagation.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/4909499/4811948/4811948-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Mean absolute distance error caused by <b>noise and multipath propagation</b> for 2FCW <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">(N_{c}=2)</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-178-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-178">(N_{c}=2)</script></tex-math></inline-formula>: tag detuned by +100% of the optimal impedance, light multipath channel; carrier offset frequencies <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f_{n}=0, 10</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-179-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-179">f_{n}=0, 10</script></tex-math></inline-formula> MHz.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/4811948/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec7"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION VII.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A linearized model of the time-variant nonlinear reflection coefficient of a passive UHF RFID tag was introduced in this paper. This model was designed for the EPCglobal Class-1 Gen-2 protocol standard <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_7">[10]</a>, but is also applicable to other types of RFID transponders using backscatter modulation. The 2FCW radar ranging approach for UHF RFID presented in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_7">[2]</a> was generalized to an arbitrary amount of carriers, utilizing an improved method of component selection. The resulting system was analyzed for vulnerabilities to systematic and stochastic errors. Performance bounds for AWGN and multipath propagation channels were derived accordingly. The theoretical results were verified by extensive simulations using a wideband UHF RFID simulator <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_7">[8]</a>.</p><p>It has been found that the system, while being vulnerable to multipath propagation (like any narrowband system), still performs well for typical RFID channels. The mean average error can be kept below 20% at distances from 0.75 m up to 4 m in such channels for the worst case of identical reader RX/TX-antennas. Using distinct antennas, the error can be kept well below 15% within the same range.</p><p>Detuning is a problem at short ranges and in nonfading channels. Simulations have shown that the MAE can exceed 50 cm for “unlucky” detuning, shifting the resonance exactly to the tag's operating point. The mean MAE for detuning in the range of −70% to 400% of the optimal impedance does not exceed 10 cm. Compensation of this error is not possible due to large variations caused by the detuning.</p><p>Finally, it has also been found that there is no gain in using more than one secondary carrier within the coherence bandwidth of the channel. As mentioned above, the systematic error caused by detuning could not be compensated using multiple carriers. Additionally, the estimate's variance cannot be improved using multiple secondary carriers inside the coherence bandwidth: In this case, the error caused by multipath propagation solely depends on the average carrier spacing, with smaller errors for larger offsets. If the 2FCW system uses the largest spacing, the variance for higher order systems is always greater than the 2FCW's variance. For AWGN channels, a similar relationship has been shown in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a>. Thus, the best achievable MAE is obtained when using 2FCW ranging with the highest possible frequency offset. Consequently, 2FCW radar is the recommended choice for narrowband ranging. Placing 2FCW carrier pairs well outside the respective coherence bandwidths will create independent fading and, thus, mitigate multipath propagation effects—at the cost of a considerably larger overall bandwidth.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

The proposed system concept relies on exact phase information; hence, the passive tag cannot be accurately modeled as a frequency-flat linear device. A linearized model of the tag's reflection coefficient is devised to bridge the gap between the nonlinear reality and the linear CW radar theory. Estimation error bounds are derived and effects caused by noise and multipath propagation are analyzed in detail. It has been found that systematic errors introduced by the tag's reflection characteristic cannot be compensated by using multiple carriers due to large variations caused by detuning. Nonetheless the system, while being vulnerable to multipath propagation effects, still performs well under line-of-sight conditions; mean average errors below 15% of the true distance are possible in
